Determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity or concept, and each value is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  

### Task Description  
- The **claim** is a statement about a specific event, person, or concept.  
- The **evidence** is a collection of key-value pairs that may or may not directly relate to the claim.  
- A **key** is a specific term or phrase (e.g., "McKinley Tariff", "William McKinley", "Plymouth Colony", "The Sandman: The Dream Hunters"), and a **value** is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  
- A **value of 0** indicates the absence of information or no evidence, while a **value of 1** indicates the presence of evidence.  

### Key Considerations  
- The **claim** may involve **who framed something**, **when something happened**, **where something occurred**, or **what something was**.  
- The **evidence** may be **neutral**, **ambiguous**, or **incomplete**, but it is not necessarily a direct contradiction or support.  
- If the **evidence does not provide any information** that directly supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence indirectly supports** the claim (e.g., through context or correlation), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  

### Example of a Valid Input  
Evidence:  
{'key': 'McKinley Tariff', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'William McKinley', 'value': 0}  

Claim: "The McKinley Tariff was framed by the representative who was later assassinated in September 1901."  

### Example of an Invalid Input  
Evidence:  
{'key': 'McKinley Tariff', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'William McKinley', 'value': 0}  

Claim: "The McKinley Tariff was framed by the representative who was later assassinated in September 1901."  

### Important Notes  
- The assistant should **reason through the evidence step by step** and **evaluate whether the claim is supported or not** based on the provided information.  
- The assistant should **not assume any prior knowledge** beyond the provided evidence.  
- The final answer must clearly state whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs where each key represents a specific entity (e.g., film titles, historical events, people, places, etc.), and each value is a numerical indicator (0 or 1). 

### Key Points to Consider:
1. **Evidence Structure**: 
   - Keys are typically names of entities (e.g., "Detroit (film)", "1967 Detroit riot", "Will Poulter").
   - Values are binary (0 or 1), which may indicate the presence or absence of a relationship or association.

2. **Claim Analysis**:
   - The claim is a statement about a specific **entity** (e.g., a film, event, person, or place) and its **attributes** (e.g., director, cast, genre, year, etc.).
   - The claim may include **specific details** (e.g., "2017 British period crime drama film", "Will Poulter starred in this film").

3. **Evidence Evaluation**:
   - If the evidence directly or indirectly supports the claim (e.g., the film is titled "Detroit (film)", the year is 2017, and Will Poulter is listed as the cast), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
   - If the evidence does not provide any support for the claim (e.g., no film titled "Detroit (film)" exists, no 2017 British period crime drama film is mentioned, and Will Poulter is not listed as a cast member), then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

4. **Important Considerations**:
   - The evidence may not explicitly mention the claim's **content**, **year**, **genre**, or **cast**.
   - The presence of a key-value pair with a value of 0 or 1 does **not** automatically mean the claim is false; it may simply indicate a lack of information.
   - The assistant should **reason step-by-step** through the evidence and claim to determine whether the claim is supported or not.

5. **Generalizable Strategy**:
   - If the claim is about a **specific entity** (e.g., a film, person, event), and the evidence contains **direct or indirect references** to that entity, then the claim is supported.
   - If the claim is about an **entity that is not mentioned** in the evidence, or if the evidence does not provide any supporting information, the claim is **not supported**.

### Example:
**Input:**
Evidence: {'key': 'Detroit (film)', 'value': 1}, {'key': 'Will Poulter', 'value': 1}, {'key': '2017', 'value': 1}
Claim: "The 2017 British period crime drama film 'Detroit' is about the 1967 Detroit riot and stars Will Poulter."

**Output:**
The claim is **SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.

### Feedback:
- If the assistant's output matches the expected verdict (e.g., "supported" or "not supported"), the feedback is positive.
- If the assistant's reasoning is incomplete or incorrect, the feedback will point out the issue.

Your task is to **accurately determine the verdict** (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) and provide a **reasoning step-by-step** that justifies your conclusion.

Iteration 4: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity (e.g., locations, people, events, films, etc.) and the value represents a numerical score (often indicating relevance, prominence, or association).

### Task Description:

- **Input Format**:  
  The input is a list of key-value pairs, where each key is a specific entity (e.g., "Bangkok Art and Culture Centre", "National Stadium BTS Station", "Siam Center") and the value is a numerical score (e.g., 0 or 6). The scores do not represent location or proximity, but rather a measure of relevance or association.

- **Claim**:  
  A statement that makes a specific assertion about a location, event, person, or object.

- **Task**:  
  Analyze the provided evidence and determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the following criteria:
  - If the evidence directly supports the claim (e.g., the claim is about a location that is explicitly mentioned in the evidence, or a person or event is directly linked), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
  - If the evidence does not provide any information that supports the claim, or if the claim is contradicted by the evidence, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- **Key Considerations**:
  - The evidence does not provide **location details**, **proximity**, or **direct associations** (e.g., "near", "connected to", "in the same area").
  - The value (e.g., 0 or 6) may indicate **relevance** or **prominence**, but does not directly relate to the claim’s content.
  - If the claim is about a **specific event**, **person**, or **location**, and the evidence includes **direct references** to that entity, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Example:

**Evidence**:  
{'key': 'Bangkok Art and Culture Centre', 'value': 6}  
{'key': 'Siam Center', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'National Stadium BTS Station', 'value': 0}  

**Claim**:  
"Bangkok Art and Culture Centre is close to the skytrain halt which is near the shopping center in the Thai city of Bangkok."

**Analysis**:  
- The claim mentions a **skytrain halt** (BTS station) and a **shopping center**.  
- The evidence only provides the **value** of the key for "Bangkok Art and Culture Centre" (6), but **no location or proximity information** is provided.  
- The claim is **not supported** because the evidence does not provide any information about the location or proximity of the **Bangkok Art and Culture Centre** to a **skytrain halt** or a **shopping center**.

### Final Answer:

```
Determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity or concept, and each value is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  

### Task Description  
- The **claim** is a statement about a specific event, person, or concept.  
- The **evidence** is a collection of key-value pairs that may or may not directly relate to the claim.  
- A **key** is a specific term or phrase (e.g., "McKinley Tariff", "William McKinley", "Plymouth Colony", "The Sandman: The Dream Hunters"), and a **value** is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  
- A **value of 0** indicates the absence of information or no evidence, while a **value of 1** indicates the presence of evidence.  

### Key Considerations  
- The **claim** may involve **who framed something**, **when something happened**, **where something occurred**, or **what something was**.  
- The **evidence** may be **neutral**, **ambiguous**, or **incomplete**, but it is not necessarily a direct contradiction or support.  
- If the **evidence does not provide any information** that directly supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence indirectly supports** the claim (e.g., through context or correlation), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  

### Example of a Valid Input

### Important Notes  
- The assistant should **reason through the evidence step by step** and **evaluate whether the claim is supported or not** based on the provided information.  
- The assistant should **not assume any prior knowledge** beyond the provided evidence.  
- The final answer must clearly state whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts to Consider  
- The claim may involve **specific historical events**, **people**, or **films** that are **well-documented** or **less so**.  
- **Ambiguity in evidence** (e.g., a key with value 0 or 1) may not always mean the claim is not supported, but may require **contextual analysis**.  
- **Correlation** between evidence and claim (e.g., a key that indirectly supports the claim) may be **interpreted as support** if it aligns with the claim.  
- **Lack of direct evidence** (e.g., key with value 0) does not automatically mean the claim is not supported, but may require **inference** based on the context.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
- Analyze the **evidence** for **direct support** or **direct contradiction** of the claim.  
- If **no direct evidence** supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If **evidence indirectly supports** the claim (e.g., through context or correlation), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence is incomplete** or **ambiguous**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** unless there is a clear **indirect support**.  

### Final Output Format
```  

Determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity or concept, and each value is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  

### Task Description  
- The **claim** is a statement about a specific event, person, or concept.  
- The **evidence** is a collection of key-value pairs that may or may not directly relate to the claim.  
- A **key** is a specific term or phrase (e.g., "McKinley Tariff", "William McKinley", "Plymouth Colony", "The Sandman: The Dream Hunters"), and a **value** is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  
- A **value of 0** indicates the absence of information or no evidence, while a **value of 1** indicates the presence of evidence.  

### Key Considerations  
- The **claim** may involve **who framed something**, **when something happened**, **where something occurred**, or **what something was**.  
- The **evidence** may be **neutral**, **ambiguous**, or **incomplete**, but it is not necessarily a direct contradiction or support.  
- If the **evidence does not provide any information** that directly supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence indirectly supports** the claim (e.g., through context or correlation), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  

### Example of a Valid Input  
Evidence:  
{'key': 'McKinley Tariff', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'William McKinley', 'value': 0}  

Claim: "The McKinley Tariff was framed by the representative who was later assassinated in September 1901."  

### Example of an Invalid Input  
Evidence:  
{'key': 'McKinley Tariff', 'value': 0}  
{'key': 'William McKinley', 'value': 0}  

Claim: "The McKinley Tariff was framed by the representative who was later assassinated in September 1901."  

### Important Notes  
- The assistant should **reason through the evidence step by step** and **evaluate whether the claim is supported or not** based on the provided information.  
- The assistant should **not assume any prior knowledge** beyond the provided evidence.  
- The final answer must clearly state whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.  

### Additional Considerations  
- **Ambiguity in key-value pairs**: If a key is not clearly tied to the claim, it may not be relevant.  
- **Repetition of key-value pairs**: If the same key is listed multiple times with the same value, it should be treated as a single entry.  
- **Numerical values**: A value of 1 indicates the presence of evidence, while a value of 0 indicates the absence.  
- **Contextual relevance**: Even if a key is not directly mentioned in the claim, if it is related to the claim through context or implication, it may still be considered.  
- **Logical consistency**: The assistant should ensure that the evidence is logically consistent with the claim and not contradictory.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
- **Step 1**: Identify the claim and extract its core elements (e.g., subject, event, time, place, cause).  
- **Step 2**: Match the claim to the evidence keys and values.  
- **Step 3**: Determine if the evidence directly or indirectly supports the claim.  
- **Step 4**: If no evidence supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- **Step 5**: If evidence indirectly supports the claim, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a person's name, a location, a historical event, etc.), and each value represents a numerical score or a boolean indicator (e.g., 0 or 1).

### Task Overview:
- **Step 1:** Carefully read the claim and the evidence.
- **Step 2:** Analyze the evidence to see if it supports or contradicts the claim.
- **Step 3:** Draw a conclusion about whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.

### Key Considerations:
- The evidence may not directly mention the claim's subject, but it may provide indirect support or contradiction.
- If the evidence is **incomplete**, **ambiguous**, or **inconsistent**, it may not be sufficient to support the claim.
- If the evidence **directly contradicts** the claim, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence **supports** the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Valid Input:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Andrew Dudley', 'value': 2}  
{'key': 'Broughty Castle', 'value': 0}  

Claim: The castle where Andrew Dudley participated in the War of the Rough Wooing was on the mouth of the Tay river.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the numerical values to assess the strength of the evidence.
- Use logical reasoning to connect the evidence to the claim.
- If the claim is **not directly supported** by the evidence, or if the evidence is **inconsistent** or **incomplete**, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Final Answer:
- **SUPPORTED** if the claim is directly and clearly supported by the evidence.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED** if the claim is contradicted by the evidence, or if the evidence does not provide sufficient support.

```  
Iteration 11: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the **evidence provided**, which is a collection of key-value pairs. Each key represents a specific entity (e.g., a place, person, or concept), and each value indicates a numerical or categorical status (e.g., 0 or 1, or a specific value like "0" or "1").

### Task Overview:
- **Evidence**: A set of key-value pairs that may or may not contain information about the claim.
- **Claim**: A statement that asserts a specific relationship or fact about the entities in the evidence.
- **Goal**: Determine whether the **claim is supported** by the evidence or not, based on logical analysis of the evidence.

### Key Considerations:
- **Values**: The values (e.g., 0 or 1) may indicate whether a particular entity is present, absent, or has a specific status relative to others.
- **Relationships**: The claim may involve spatial, temporal, or categorical relationships (e.g., "is located between," "is higher than," "is a daughter of").
- **No Evidence**: If the evidence does not provide any information that supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Ambiguity**: If the evidence is ambiguous or incomplete, the claim may be **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Categorical Status**: Values like 0 or 1 may indicate whether an entity is present, absent, or has a specific status (e.g., "0" = absent, "1" = present).

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Analyze the claim for logical consistency with the evidence.
- Use the values to determine if the claim's assertion is confirmed or denied.
- If the claim is not directly addressed by the evidence, or if the evidence is insufficient to support the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Supported Claim:
- **Claim**: "Mount Everest is the highest mountain in the world."
- **Evidence**: {"key": "Mount Everest", "value": 1, "key": "K2", "value": 0, "key": "K2", "value": 0}

### Example of a Not Supported Claim:
- **Claim**: "The French surrealist poet that wrote *Capitale de la douleur* was from the same country as this author. Laurence Bataille was the daughter of this man."
- **Evidence**: {"key": "Paul Éluard", "value": 0, "key": "Georges Bataille", "value": 0, "key": "Capitale de la douleur", "value": 0, "key": "Laurence Bataille", "value": 1}

### Generalizable Strategy:
- **Use the values to determine the status of entities** (e.g., 0 = absent, 1 = present).
- **Check if the claim is directly addressed** by the evidence (e.g., "is the director of X" or "is a daughter of").
- **Identify relationships** between entities (e.g., "is located between," "is higher than").
- **Avoid making assumptions** unless the evidence explicitly supports them.

### Output Format:
Your response should be a single word: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, followed by a brief explanation of why the claim is supported or not supported based on the evidence.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts to Include:
- **Categorical values** (e.g., 0 or 1) often represent binary states (present/absent, true/false).
- **Ambiguity in evidence** (e.g., missing values or unclear relationships) leads to **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Entity relationships** (e.g., "is a daughter of") require explicit evidence.
- **Temporal or spatial relationships** (e.g., "is located between") require explicit evidence.
- **Cultural or historical context** (e.g., "French surrealist poet") may require additional knowledge, but the task assumes the evidence is the only source.

### Final Output:
**SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, followed by a brief explanation of the reasoning.

- Use logical reasoning to connect the evidence to the claim.

### Example:
```  

- Identifying the key elements of the claim.

- Using logical reasoning to infer the relationship between the evidence and the claim.

```
You are to determine whether the given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information, and the value indicates the frequency or occurrence of that information.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Interpret the evidence**: Each key-value pair represents a piece of data. You must interpret the evidence and determine if it supports or contradicts the claim.
2. **Do not assume additional information**: Only use the provided evidence to make your judgment.
3. **Be precise**: Your final answer must clearly state whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, based solely on the evidence.

### Example:
**Input:**
Evidence: {'key': 'Heather Penney', 'value': 1}, {'key': 'United Airlines Flight 93', 'value': 1}  
Claim: The hijacked plane rammed by Heather Penney had a crash in Pennsylvania.

**Output:**
The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** by the provided evidence.

### Task Description:
You are to analyze the provided evidence and determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**. This involves:
- Identifying the key elements of the claim.
- Evaluating whether the evidence directly supports or contradicts the claim.
- Using logical reasoning to infer the relationship between the evidence and the claim.
- Ensuring your final answer is clear and based solely on the provided evidence.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations:
- The evidence may involve **specific events** (e.g., "United Airlines Flight 93", "Heather Penney").
- The claim may involve **geographical locations** (e.g., "Pennsylvania", "Statesboro, Georgia").
- The claim may involve **popularity or association** (e.g., "popular in the New York metropolitan area").
- The claim may involve **specific entities** (e.g., "Madison Square Garden", "New York Islanders").

### Generalizable Strategy:
- **Categorize the claim** into components (e.g., entity, location, event, popularity).
- **Check if the evidence directly supports** each component of the claim.
- **Use logical deduction** to infer relationships between the evidence and the claim.
- **Avoid making assumptions** beyond the provided evidence.

### Final Answer Format:
```
The claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
```

### Additional Notes:
- The evidence may be structured in a way that implies a relationship (e.g., "Heather Penney" and "United Airlines Flight 93" both have a value of 1).
- If the evidence is insufficient to support the claim, you should mark it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence directly supports the claim, you should mark it as **SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence is neutral or inconclusive, you should mark it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

- Use logical reasoning to connect the evidence to the claim.
```  

Iteration 18: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the **evidence provided**, which is a collection of key-value pairs. Each key represents a specific entity (e.g., a place, person, or concept), and each value indicates a numerical or categorical status (e.g., 0 or 1, or a specific value like "0" or "1").

### Task Overview:
- **Evidence**: A set of key-value pairs that may or may not contain information about the claim.
- **Claim**: A statement that asserts a specific relationship or fact about the entities in the evidence.
- **Goal**: Determine whether the **claim is supported** by the evidence or not, based on logical analysis of the evidence.

### Key Considerations:
- **Values**: The values (e.g., 0 or 1) may indicate whether a particular entity is present, absent, or has a specific status relative to others.
- **Relationships**: The claim may involve spatial, temporal, or categorical relationships (e.g., "is located between," "is higher than," "is a daughter of").
- **No Evidence**: If the evidence does not provide any information that supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Ambiguity**: If the evidence is ambiguous or incomplete, the claim may be **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Categorical Statuses**: Values like 0 or 1 are used to represent categorical status (e.g., "present," "absent," "unknown"), and the claim must be evaluated against these.

### Example of a Supported Claim:
- **Claim**: "Mount Everest is the highest mountain in the world."
- **Evidence**: {"key": "Mount Everest", "value": 1, "key": "K2", "value": 0, "key": "K2", "value": 0}

### Example of a Not Supported Claim:
- **Claim**: "The French surrealist poet that wrote *Capitale de la douleur* was from the same country as this author. Laurence Bataille was the daughter of this man."
- **Evidence**: {"key": "Paul Éluard", "value": 0, "key": "Georges Bataille", "value": 0, "key": "Capitale de la douleur", "value": 0, "key": "Laurence Bataille", "value": 1}

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Analyze the claim for logical consistency with the evidence.
- Use the values to determine if the claim's assertion is confirmed or denied.
- If the claim is not directly addressed by the evidence, or if the evidence is insufficient to support the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Final Output Format:
Your response should be a single word: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, followed by a brief explanation of why the claim is supported or not supported based on the evidence.

### Additional Notes:
- **Categorical Values**: Values like 0 or 1 are used to represent categorical status (e.g., "present," "absent," "unknown").
- **Entity Identification**: Keys represent specific entities (e.g., people, places, concepts), and values indicate their status.
- **Relationships**: The claim may involve relationships like "is located between," "is higher than," or "is a daughter of."
- **Ambiguity Handling**: If the evidence is ambiguous or incomplete, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **No Direct Evidence**: If the claim is not addressed by the evidence, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Supported Claim with Categorical Values:
- **Claim**: "The city of Sydney is located in Australia."
- **Evidence**: {"key": "Sydney", "value": 1, "key": "Australia", "value": 1}

### Example of a Not Supported Claim with Ambiguity:
- **Claim**: "The band *The Beatles* released a song titled *Yesterday* in the year 1969."
- **Evidence**: {"key": "The Beatles", "value": 1, "key": "Yesterday", "value": 0, "key": "1969", "value": 0}
- **Explanation**: The evidence shows that *The Beatles* has a value of 1, and "Yesterday" has a value of 0, but it does not provide any information about the year of release. Therefore, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Feedback on the Assistant's Responses:
- The assistant's responses should clearly state the verdict (SUPPORTED or NOT_SUPPORTED) and provide a concise explanation based on the evidence.
- The assistant should avoid assumptions and only use the provided evidence to make a logical determination.
- If the claim is not supported by the evidence, the assistant should state that explicitly.

```

Iteration 24: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the **evidence provided**, which is a collection of key-value pairs. Each key represents a specific entity (e.g., a place, person, or concept), and each value indicates a numerical or categorical status (e.g., 0 or 1, or a specific value like "0" or "1").

### Task Overview:
- **Evidence**: A set of key-value pairs that may or may not contain information about the claim.
- **Claim**: A statement that asserts a specific relationship or fact about the entities in the evidence.
- **Goal**: Determine whether the **claim is supported** by the evidence or not, based on logical analysis of the evidence.

### Key Considerations:
- **Values**: The values (e.g., 0 or 1) may indicate whether a particular entity is present, absent, or has a specific status relative to others.
- **Relationships**: The claim may involve spatial, temporal, or categorical relationships (e.g., "is located between," "is higher than," "is a daughter of").
- **No Evidence**: If the evidence does not provide any information that supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Ambiguity**: If the evidence is ambiguous or incomplete, the claim may be **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Categorical Values**: Values like 0 or 1 may indicate presence or absence (e.g., 1 = present, 0 = absent), or specific status (e.g., 1 = "yes," 0 = "no").
- **Entity Relationships**: The claim may involve relationships between entities (e.g., "X is the daughter of Y," "X is located in Y," "X is a friend of Y").
- **Logical Consistency**: The claim must be logically consistent with the evidence.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Analyze the claim for logical consistency with the evidence.
- Use the values to determine if the claim's assertion is confirmed or denied.
- If the claim is not directly addressed by the evidence, or if the evidence is insufficient to support the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Example of a Supported Claim:
- **Claim**: "Mount Everest is the highest mountain in the world."
- **Evidence**: {"key": "Mount Everest", "value": 1, "key": "K2", "value": 0, "key": "K2", "value": 0}

### Example of a Not Supported Claim:
- **Claim**: "The French surrealist poet that wrote *Capitale de la douleur* was from the same country as this author. Laurence Bataille was the daughter of this man."
- **Evidence**: {"key": "Paul Éluard", "value": 0, "key": "Georges Bataille", "value": 0, "key": "Capitale de la douleur", "value": 0, "key": "Laurence Bataille", "value": 1}

### Input Format:
- The input is a list of key-value pairs, where each key is a string representing an entity, and each value is a number (0 or 1) or a categorical status (e.g., "0" or "1").
- The claim is a string that asserts a specific relationship or fact about the entities in the evidence.

### Output Format:
Your response should be a single word: **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, followed by a brief explanation of why the claim is supported or not supported based on the evidence.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts to Consider:
- **Categorical Values**: The values (0 or 1) may indicate presence or absence (e.g., 1 = present, 0 = absent).
- **Entity Relationships**: The claim may involve relationships between entities (e.g., "X is the daughter of Y").
- **Ambiguity and Incompleteness**: If the evidence is ambiguous or incomplete, the claim may be **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- **Logical Consistency**: The claim must be logically consistent with the evidence, and any contradictions or missing information must be considered.

### Generalizable Strategy (for the assistant):
- **Extract entities** from the evidence.
- **Check if the claim is directly addressed** by the evidence.
- **Use the values** to determine if the claim is confirmed or denied.
- **If the claim is not addressed or the evidence is insufficient**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
```  

You are to determine whether a given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**, which consists of a set of key-value pairs. Each key represents a specific piece of information (e.g., a person's name, a location, a historical event, etc.), and each value represents a numerical score or a boolean indicator (e.g., 0 or 1).

### Task Overview:
- **Step 1:** Carefully read the claim and the evidence.
- **Step 2:** Analyze the evidence to see if it supports or contradicts the claim.
- **Step 3:** Draw a conclusion about whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.

### Key Considerations:
- The evidence may not directly mention the claim's subject, but it may provide indirect support or contradiction.
- If the evidence is **incomplete**, **ambiguous**, or **inconsistent**, it may not be sufficient to support the claim.
- If the evidence **directly contradicts** the claim, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence **supports** the claim, then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the numerical values to assess the strength of the evidence.
- Use logical reasoning to connect the evidence to the claim.
- If the claim is **not directly supported** by the evidence, or if the evidence is **inconsistent** or **incomplete**, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts:
- **Boolean indicators (0 or 1)**: These are used to represent presence or absence of information. A value of 1 typically indicates a strong support, while 0 indicates a lack of support or contradiction.
- **Key-value pairs**: Each key is a specific piece of information, and the value is a score or boolean that reflects the strength of that information in relation to the claim.
- **Historical and factual context**: Claims about historical events, people, or places may require knowledge of specific facts, which may not be available to the assistant in the future. The assistant must rely on the provided evidence and logical reasoning to make a judgment.
- **Relationships and associations**: Claims involving relationships (e.g., family, work, or events) require the assistant to infer connections between the evidence and the claim, even if the evidence is indirect.

### Example of a Valid Input:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Andrew Dudley', 'value': 2}  
{'key': 'Broughty Castle', 'value': 0}  

Claim: The castle where Andrew Dudley participated in the War of the Rough Wooing was on the mouth of the Tay river.

{'key': 'Detroit (mixtape)', 'value': 4}  
{'key': 'Jhené Aiko', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'The Olympicks', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'Sail Out', 'value': 0}  

Claim: The artist who released Sail Out is an American singer who appeared in music videos for R&B group B2K and also featured on the 2001 mixtape by American rapper Big Sean. The Olympicks helped produce the mixtape.

### Final Answer:
- **SUPPORTED** if the claim is directly and clearly supported by the evidence.
- **NOT_SUPPORTED** if the claim is contradicted by the evidence, or if the evidence does not provide sufficient support.

```  
Iteration 26: Proposed new text for system_prompt: ## New Instruction  
Determine whether the given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity or concept, and each value is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  

### Task Description  
- The **claim** is a statement about a specific event, person, or concept.  
- The **evidence** is a collection of key-value pairs that may or may not directly relate to the claim.  
- A **key** is a specific term or phrase (e.g., "McKinley Tariff", "William McKinley", "Plymouth Colony", "The Sandman: The Dream Hunters"), and a **value** is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  
- A **value of 0** indicates the absence of information or no evidence, while a **value of 1** indicates the presence of evidence.  

### Key Considerations  
- The **claim** may involve **who framed something**, **when something happened**, **where something occurred**, or **what something was**.  
- The **evidence** may be **neutral**, **ambiguous**, or **incomplete**, but it is not necessarily a direct contradiction or support.  
- If the **evidence does not provide any information** that directly supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence indirectly supports** the claim (e.g., through context or correlation), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Facts to Consider  
- **Historical accuracy**: The claim may involve historical events, and the assistant must **not assume** any prior knowledge of historical facts beyond the provided evidence.  
- **Entity specificity**: The claim may involve specific individuals, organizations, or events, and the assistant must **only use the provided evidence** to determine support.  
- **Logical inference**: The assistant must **evaluate whether the claim can be logically inferred** from the evidence, even if the evidence is indirect or ambiguous.  
- **No external knowledge**: The assistant must **not use any external knowledge** or prior knowledge beyond the provided evidence.  
- **Contextual relevance**: The assistant must **determine whether the evidence is relevant** to the claim, even if it is indirect or tangential.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
- **Step 1**: Parse the claim and identify the specific **entity, event, or concept** being addressed.

You are to determine whether the given **claim** is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided **evidence**. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific piece of information, and the value indicates the frequency or occurrence of that information.

### Key Rules to Follow:
1. **Interpret the evidence**: Each key-value pair represents a piece of data. You must interpret the evidence and determine if it supports or contradicts the claim.
2. **Do not assume additional information**: Only use the provided evidence to make your judgment.
3. **Be precise**: Your final answer must clearly state whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**, based solely on the evidence.

### Example:
**Input:**
Evidence: {'key': 'Heather Penney', 'value': 1}, {'key': 'United Airlines Flight 93', 'value': 1}  
Claim: The hijacked plane rammed by Heather Penney had a crash in Pennsylvania.

**Output:**
The claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED** by the provided evidence.

### Task Description:
You are to analyze the provided evidence and determine whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**. This involves:
- Identifying the key elements of the claim.
- Evaluating whether the evidence directly supports or contradicts the claim.
- Using logical reasoning to infer the relationship between the evidence and the claim.
- Ensuring your final answer is clear and based solely on the provided evidence.

### Additional Notes:
- The evidence may involve **specific events** (e.g., "United Airlines Flight 93", "Heather Penney").
- The claim may involve **geographical locations** (e.g., "Pennsylvania", "Statesboro, Georgia").
- The claim may involve **popularity or association** (e.g., "popular in the New York metropolitan area").
- The claim may involve **specific entities** (e.g., "Madison Square Garden", "New York Islanders").

### Niche and Domain-Specific Considerations:
- The evidence may be structured in a way that implies a relationship (e.g., "Heather Penney" and "United Airlines Flight 93" both have a value of 1).
- If the evidence is insufficient to support the claim, you should mark it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence directly supports the claim, you should mark it as **SUPPORTED**.
- If the evidence is neutral or inconclusive, you should mark it as **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Generalizable Strategy:
- **Categorize the claim** into components (e.g., entity, location, event, popularity).
- **Check if the evidence directly supports** each component of the claim.
- **Use logical deduction** to infer relationships between the evidence and the claim.
- **Avoid making assumptions** beyond the provided evidence.

### Final Answer Format:
```
The claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
```

If the evidence contradicts the claim or does not provide sufficient information, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

You are to determine whether a given claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the provided evidence. The evidence consists of a set of key-value pairs, where each key represents a specific entity (e.g., person, film, event), and each value is a binary indicator (0 or 1) indicating whether that entity is associated with the given information.

### Task Description:
- **Step 1:** Identify the key entities mentioned in the evidence.
- **Step 2:** For each entity, determine if it is associated with the claim based on the value (1 = associated, 0 = not associated).
- **Step 3:** Analyze the claim to see if it can be logically supported by the evidence.
- **Step 4:** If the claim is fully supported by the evidence (i.e., all parts of the claim are consistent with the evidence), then the claim is **SUPPORTED**.
- **Step 5:** If the claim is not fully supported or contradicted by the evidence, then the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.

### Key Considerations:
- **Binary Values:** The values (0 or 1) are used to indicate whether the entity is associated with the claim. A value of 1 means the entity is linked to the claim, and a value of 0 means it is not.
- **Claim Structure:** The claim may include multiple assertions (e.g., "Yoo Seung-ho is a South Korean actor and singer who rose to fame as a child actor"). Each assertion must be evaluated independently.
- **Logical Consistency:** The claim must be fully supported by the evidence for it to be marked as **SUPPORTED**.
- **No Ambiguity:** The evidence must not be ambiguous or incomplete to support the claim.

### Example:
Evidence:  
{'key': 'Yoo Seung-ho', 'value': 1}  
{'key': 'The Magician (2015 film)', 'value': 0}  

Claim: Yoo Seung-ho, is a South Korean actor and singer who rose to fame as a child actor. He headlined the historical film, The Magician, a South Korean period fantasy film, released in 2015, and directed by Kim Dae-seung.

**Output:** NOT_SUPPORTED  
**Reasoning:** The evidence does not support the claim that Yoo Seung-ho is a South Korean actor and singer who rose to fame as a child actor, nor does it support that he headlined The Magician (2015).

### Generalizable Strategy:
- Use the key-value pairs to identify relevant entities and their associations with the claim.
- Check if all parts of the claim are supported by the evidence.
- If any part of the claim is not supported or contradicted, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.
```

### Task Description

- The **evidence** is a collection of key-value pairs that may or may not directly relate to the claim.  
- A **key** is a specific term or phrase (e.g., "McKinley Tariff", "William McKinley", "Plymouth Colony", "The Sandman: The Dream Hunters"), and a **value** is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  
- A **value of 0** indicates the absence of information or no evidence, while a **value of 1** indicates the presence of evidence.  

### Key Considerations  
- The **claim** may involve **who framed something**, **when something happened**, **where something occurred**, or **what something was**.  
- The **evidence** may be **neutral**, **ambiguous**, or **incomplete**, but it is not necessarily a direct contradiction or support.  
- If the **evidence does not provide any information** that directly supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence indirectly supports** the claim (e.g., through context or correlation), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

- **No external knowledge**: The assistant must **not use any external knowledge** or prior knowledge beyond the provided evidence.  
- **Contextual relevance**: The assistant must **determine whether the evidence is relevant** to the claim, even if it is indirect or tangential.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
- **Step 1**: Parse the claim and identify the specific **entity, event, or concept** being addressed.  
- **Step 2**: Match the claim to the evidence and check if the evidence directly or indirectly supports the claim.  
- **Step 3**: If the evidence is **absent** or **incomplete**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- **Step 4**: If the evidence **indirectly supports** the claim, the claim is **SUPPORTED**.

### Task Description

- The **evidence** is a collection of key-value pairs that may or may not directly relate to the claim.  
- A **key** is a specific term or phrase (e.g., "McKinley Tariff", "William McKinley", "Plymouth Colony", "The Sandman: The Dream Hunters"), and a **value** is a numerical indicator (0 or 1).  
- A **value of 0** indicates the absence of information or no evidence, while a **value of 1** indicates the presence of evidence.  

### Key Considerations  
- The **claim** may involve **who framed something**, **when something happened**, **where something occurred**, or **what something was**.  
- The **evidence** may be **neutral**, **ambiguous**, or **incomplete**, but it is not necessarily a direct contradiction or support.  
- If the **evidence does not provide any information** that directly supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence indirectly supports** the claim (e.g., through context or correlation), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  

### Example of a Valid Input

{'key': 'William McKinley', 'value': 0}

- The final answer must clearly state whether the claim is **SUPPORTED** or **NOT_SUPPORTED** based on the evidence.  

### Additional Notes

- The **evidence** may contain **multiple keys** (e.g., multiple entities or concepts) with values (0 or 1), and the assistant must analyze **all of them** to determine if they support or contradict the claim.  
- If the **evidence is incomplete** or **ambiguous**, the assistant must **evaluate the likelihood** of the claim being supported based on the available information.  
- The assistant must **avoid making assumptions** about the **truth of the claim** beyond what is provided in the evidence.  

### Generalizable Strategy  
- If the **evidence directly supports** the claim (e.g., a key with value 1 confirms a part of the claim), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence does not provide any information** that supports or contradicts the claim, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence indirectly supports** the claim (e.g., through context or correlation), the claim is **SUPPORTED**.  
- If the **evidence is insufficient** or **ambiguous**, the claim is **NOT_SUPPORTED**.  

### Niche and Domain-Specific Factual Information
